<P class="p508 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">4</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">Parties that do not make extradition conditional on the existence of a treaty shall recognise the criminal offences referred to in paragraph 1 of this article as extraditable offences between themselves.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p511 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">5</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">Extradition shall be subject to the conditions provided for by the law of the requested Party or by applicable extradition treaties, including the grounds on which the requested Party may refuse extradition.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p560 ft92"><SPAN class="ft94">6</SPAN><SPAN class="ft105">If extradition for a criminal offence referred to in paragraph 1 of this article is refused solely on the basis of the nationality of the person sought, or because the requested Party deems that it has jurisdiction over the offence, the requested Party shall submit the case at the request of the requesting Party to its competent authorities for the purpose of prosecution and shall report the final outcome to the requesting Party in due course. Those authorities shall take their decision and conduct their investigations and proceedings in the same manner as for any other offence of a comparable nature under the law of that Party.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p561 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">7</SPAN><SPAN class="ft106">a </SPAN>Each Party shall, at the time of signature or when depositing its instrument of ratification, acceptance, approval or accession, communicate to the Secretary General of the Council of Europe the name and address of each authority responsible for making or receiving requests for extradition or provisional arrest in the absence of a treaty.</P>
<P class="p562 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">b</SPAN><SPAN class="ft95">The Secretary General of the Council of Europe shall set up and keep updated a register of authorities so designated by the Parties. Each Party shall ensure that the details held on the register are correct at all times.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p563 ft91">Title 3 – General principles relating to mutual assistance</P>
<P class="p475 ft86">Article 25 – General principles relating to mutual assistance</P>
<P class="p494 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">1</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">The Parties shall afford one another mutual assistance to the widest extent possible for the purpose of investigations or proceedings concerning criminal offences related to computer systems and data, or for the collection of evidence in electronic form of a criminal offence.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p564 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">2</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">Each Party shall also adopt such legislative and other measures as may be necessary to carry out the obligations set forth in Articles 27 through 35.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p565 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">3</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">Each Party may, in urgent circumstances, make requests for mutual assistance or communications related thereto by expedited means of communication, including fax or e- mail, to the extent that such means provide appropriate levels of security and authentication (including the use of encryption, where necessary), with formal confirmation to follow, where required by the requested Party. The requested Party shall accept and respond to the request by any such expedited means of communication.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p566 ft92"><SPAN class="ft94">4</SPAN><SPAN class="ft105">Except as otherwise specifically provided in articles in this chapter, mutual assistance shall be subject to the conditions provided for by the law of the requested Party or by applicable mutual assistance treaties, including the grounds on which the requested Party may refuse </SPAN><NOBR>co-operation.</NOBR> The requested Party shall not exercise the right to refuse mutual assistance in relation to the offences referred to in Articles 2 through 11 solely on the ground that the request concerns an offence which it considers a fiscal offence.</P>
<P class="p508 ft92"><SPAN class="ft94">5</SPAN><SPAN class="ft105">Where, in accordance with the provisions of this chapter, the requested Party is permitted to make mutual assistance conditional upon the existence of dual criminality, that condition shall be deemed fulfilled, irrespective of whether its laws place the offence within the same category of offence or denominate the offence by the same terminology as the requesting Party, if the conduct underlying the offence for which assistance is sought is a criminal offence under its laws.</SPAN></P>
</DIV>
<DIV id="id_2">
<P class="p164 ft2">92</P>
</DIV>
</DIV>
<DIV id="page_93">


<DIV id="id_1">
<P class="p452 ft2">Prop. 2020/21:72</P>
<P class="p453 ft2">Bilaga 1</P>
<P class="p454 ft93">ETS 185 – Cybercrime (Convention), 23.XI.2001</P>
<P class="p455 ft93">__________________________________________________________________________________</P>
<P class="p476 ft86">Article 26 – Spontaneous information</P>
<P class="p503 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">1</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">A Party may, within the limits of its domestic law and without prior request, forward to another Party information obtained within the framework of its own investigations when it considers that the disclosure of such information might assist the receiving Party in initiating or carrying out investigations or proceedings concerning criminal offences established in accordance with this Convention or might lead to a request for </SPAN><NOBR>co-operation</NOBR> by that Party under this chapter.</P>
<P class="p523 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">2</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">Prior to providing such information, the providing Party may request that it be kept confidential or only used subject to conditions. If the receiving Party cannot comply with such request, it shall notify the providing Party, which shall then determine whether the information should nevertheless be provided. If the receiving Party accepts the information subject to the conditions, it shall be bound by them.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p567 ft91">Title 4 – Procedures pertaining to mutual assistance requests</P>
<P class="p568 ft91">in the absence of applicable international agreements</P>
<P class="p569 ft113">Article 27 – Procedures pertaining to mutual assistance requests in the absence of applicable international agreements</P>
<P class="p535 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">1</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">Where there is no mutual assistance treaty or arrangement on the basis of uniform or reciprocal legislation in force between the requesting and requested Parties, the provisions of paragraphs 2 through 9 of this article shall apply. The provisions of this article shall not apply where such treaty, arrangement or legislation exists, unless the Parties concerned agree to apply any or all of the remainder of this article in lieu thereof.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p570 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">2</SPAN><SPAN class="ft114">a </SPAN>Each Party shall designate a central authority or authorities responsible for sending and answering requests for mutual assistance, the execution of such requests or their transmission to the authorities competent for their execution.</P>
<P class="p571 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">b</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">The central authorities shall communicate directly with each other;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p516 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">c</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">Each Party shall, at the time of signature or when depositing its instrument of ratification, acceptance, approval or accession, communicate to the Secretary General of the Council of Europe the names and addresses of the authorities designated in pursuance of this paragraph;</SPAN></P>
<P class="p558 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">d</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">The Secretary General of the Council of Europe shall set up and keep updated a register of central authorities designated by the Parties. Each Party shall ensure that the details held on the register are correct at all times.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p572 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">3</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">Mutual assistance requests under this article shall be executed in accordance with the procedures specified by the requesting Party, except where incompatible with the law of the requested Party.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p573 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">4</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">The requested Party may, in addition to the grounds for refusal established in Article 25, paragraph 4, refuse assistance if:</SPAN></P>
<P class="p574 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">a </SPAN>the request concerns an offence which the requested Party considers a political offence or an offence connected with a political offence, or</P>
<P class="p539 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">b </SPAN>it considers that execution of the request is likely to prejudice its sovereignty, security, <SPAN class="ft91">ordre public </SPAN>or other essential interests.</P>
<P class="p575 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">5</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">The requested Party may postpone action on a request if such action would prejudice criminal investigations or proceedings conducted by its authorities.</SPAN></P>
</DIV>
<DIV id="id_2">
<P class="p164 ft2">93</P>
</DIV>
</DIV>
<DIV id="page_94">


<DIV id="id_1">
<P class="p164 ft2">Prop. 2020/21:72</P>
<P class="p440 ft2">Bilaga 1</P>
<P class="p463 ft93">ETS 185 – Cybercrime (Convention), 23.XI.2001</P>
<P class="p464 ft93">__________________________________________________________________________________</P>
<P class="p508 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">6</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">Before refusing or postponing assistance, the requested Party shall, where appropriate after having consulted with the requesting Party, consider whether the request may be granted partially or subject to such conditions as it deems necessary.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p576 ft116"><SPAN class="ft94">7</SPAN><SPAN class="ft115">The requested Party shall promptly inform the requesting Party of the outcome of the execution of a request for assistance. Reasons shall be given for any refusal or postponement of the request. The requested Party shall also inform the requesting Party of any reasons that render impossible the execution of the request or are likely to delay it significantly.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p511 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">8</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">The requesting Party may request that the requested Party keep confidential the fact of any request made under this chapter as well as its subject, except to the extent necessary for its execution. If the requested Party cannot comply with the request for confidentiality, it shall promptly inform the requesting Party, which shall then determine whether the request should nevertheless be executed.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p577 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">9</SPAN><SPAN class="ft106">a </SPAN>In the event of urgency, requests for mutual assistance or communications related thereto may be sent directly by judicial authorities of the requesting Party to such authorities of the requested Party. In any such cases, a copy shall be sent at the same time to the central authority of the requested Party through the central authority of the requesting Party.</P>
<P class="p578 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">b</SPAN><SPAN class="ft95">Any request or communication under this paragraph may be made through the International Criminal Police Organisation (Interpol).</SPAN></P>
<P class="p466 ft90"><SPAN class="ft96">c</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">Where a request is made pursuant to </SPAN><NOBR>sub-paragraph</NOBR> a. of this article and the authority is not competent to deal with the request, it shall refer the request to the competent national authority and inform directly the requesting Party that it has done so.</P>
<P class="p466 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">d</SPAN><SPAN class="ft95">Requests or communications made under this paragraph that do not involve coercive action may be directly transmitted by the competent authorities of the requesting Party to the competent authorities of the requested Party.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p562 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">e</SPAN><SPAN class="ft95">Each Party may, at the time of signature or when depositing its instrument of ratification, acceptance, approval or accession, inform the Secretary General of the Council of Europe that, for reasons of efficiency, requests made under this paragraph are to be addressed to its central authority.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p579 ft86">Article 28 – Confidentiality and limitation on use</P>
<P class="p494 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">1</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">When there is no mutual assistance treaty or arrangement on the basis of uniform or reciprocal legislation in force between the requesting and the requested Parties, the provisions of this article shall apply. The provisions of this article shall not apply where such treaty, arrangement or legislation exists, unless the Parties concerned agree to apply any or all of the remainder of this article in lieu thereof.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p509 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">2</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">The requested Party may make the supply of information or material in response to a request dependent on the condition that it is:</SPAN></P>
<P class="p514 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">a </SPAN>kept confidential where the request for mutual legal assistance could not be complied with in the absence of such condition, or</P>
<P class="p500 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">b</SPAN><SPAN class="ft95">not used for investigations or proceedings other than those stated in the request.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p565 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">3</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">If the requesting Party cannot comply with a condition referred to in paragraph 2, it shall promptly inform the other Party, which shall then determine whether the information should nevertheless be provided. When the requesting Party accepts the condition, it shall be bound by it.</SPAN></P>
</DIV>
<DIV id="id_2">
<P class="p164 ft2">94</P>
</DIV>
</DIV>
<DIV id="page_95">


<DIV id="id_1">
<P class="p452 ft2">Prop. 2020/21:72</P>
<P class="p453 ft2">Bilaga 1</P>
<P class="p454 ft93">ETS 185 – Cybercrime (Convention), 23.XI.2001</P>
<P class="p455 ft93">__________________________________________________________________________________</P>
<P class="p580 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">4</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">Any Party that supplies information or material subject to a condition referred to in paragraph 2 may require the other Party to explain, in relation to that condition, the use made of such information or material.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p525 ft86">Section 2 – Specific provisions</P>
<P class="p581 ft91">Title 1 – Mutual assistance regarding provisional measures</P>
<P class="p476 ft86">Article 29 – Expedited preservation of stored computer data</P>
<P class="p582 ft104"><SPAN class="ft94">1</SPAN><SPAN class="ft103">A Party may request another Party to order or otherwise obtain the expeditious preservation of data stored by means of a computer system, located within the territory of that other Party and in respect of which the requesting Party intends to submit a request for mutual assistance for the search or similar access, seizure or similar securing, or disclosure of the data.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p583 ft112"><SPAN class="ft94">2</SPAN><SPAN class="ft117">A request for preservation made under paragraph 1 shall specify: </SPAN><SPAN class="ft118">a </SPAN>the authority seeking the preservation;</P>
<P class="p584 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">b </SPAN>the offence that is the subject of a criminal investigation or proceedings and a brief summary of the related facts;</P>
<P class="p479 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">c </SPAN>the stored computer data to be preserved and its relationship to the offence;</P>
<P class="p585 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">d </SPAN>any available information identifying the custodian of the stored computer data or the location of the computer system;</P>
<P class="p479 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">e </SPAN>the necessity of the preservation; and</P>
<P class="p539 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">f </SPAN>that the Party intends to submit a request for mutual assistance for the search or similar access, seizure or similar securing, or disclosure of the stored computer data.</P>
<P class="p535 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">3</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">Upon receiving the request from another Party, the requested Party shall take all appropriate measures to preserve expeditiously the specified data in accordance with its domestic law. For the purposes of responding to a request, dual criminality shall not be required as a condition to providing such preservation.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p559 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">4</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">A Party that requires dual criminality as a condition for responding to a request for mutual assistance for the search or similar access, seizure or similar securing, or disclosure of stored data may, in respect of offences other than those established in accordance with Articles 2 through 11 of this Convention, reserve the right to refuse the request for preservation under this article in cases where it has reasons to believe that at the time of disclosure the condition of dual criminality cannot be fulfilled.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p586 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">5</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">In addition, a request for preservation may only be refused if:</SPAN></P>
<P class="p585 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">a </SPAN>the request concerns an offence which the requested Party considers a political offence or an offence connected with a political offence, or</P>
<P class="p574 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">b </SPAN>the requested Party considers that execution of the request is likely to prejudice its sovereignty, security, <SPAN class="ft91">ordre public </SPAN>or other essential interests.</P>
<P class="p535 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">6</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">Where the requested Party believes that preservation will not ensure the future availability of the data or will threaten the confidentiality of or otherwise prejudice the requesting Party’s investigation, it shall promptly so inform the requesting Party, which shall then determine whether the request should nevertheless be executed.</SPAN></P>
</DIV>
<DIV id="id_2">
<P class="p164 ft2">95</P>
</DIV>
</DIV>
<DIV id="page_96">


<DIV id="id_1">
<P class="p164 ft2">Prop. 2020/21:72</P>
<P class="p440 ft2">Bilaga 1</P>
<P class="p463 ft93">ETS 185 – Cybercrime (Convention), 23.XI.2001</P>
<P class="p464 ft93">__________________________________________________________________________________</P>
<P class="p508 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">7</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">Any preservation effected in response to the request referred to in paragraph 1 shall be for a period not less than sixty days, in order to enable the requesting Party to submit a request for the search or similar access, seizure or similar securing, or disclosure of the data. Following the receipt of such a request, the data shall continue to be preserved pending a decision on that request.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p587 ft86">Article 30 – Expedited disclosure of preserved traffic data</P>
<P class="p494 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">1</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">Where, in the course of the execution of a request made pursuant to Article 29 to preserve traffic data concerning a specific communication, the requested Party discovers that a service provider in another State was involved in the transmission of the communication, the requested Party shall expeditiously disclose to the requesting Party a sufficient amount of traffic data to identify that service provider and the path through which the communication was transmitted.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p588 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">2</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">Disclosure of traffic data under paragraph 1 may only be withheld if:</SPAN></P>
<P class="p465 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">a </SPAN>the request concerns an offence which the requested Party considers a political offence or an offence connected with a political offence; or</P>
<P class="p529 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">b </SPAN>the requested Party considers that execution of the request is likely to prejudice its sovereignty, security, <SPAN class="ft91">ordre public </SPAN>or other essential interests.</P>
<P class="p589 ft91">Title 2 – Mutual assistance regarding investigative powers</P>
<P class="p475 ft86">Article 31 – Mutual assistance regarding accessing of stored computer data</P>
<P class="p494 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">1</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">A Party may request another Party to search or similarly access, seize or similarly secure, and disclose data stored by means of a computer system located within the territory of the requested Party, including data that has been preserved pursuant to Article 29.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p511 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">2</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">The requested Party shall respond to the request through the application of international instruments, arrangements and laws referred to in Article 23, and in accordance with other relevant provisions of this chapter.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p512 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">3</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">The request shall be responded to on an expedited basis where:</SPAN></P>
<P class="p514 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">a </SPAN>there are grounds to believe that relevant data is particularly vulnerable to loss or modification; or</P>
<P class="p514 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">b </SPAN>the instruments, arrangements and laws referred to in paragraph 2 otherwise provide for expedited <NOBR>co-operation.</NOBR></P>
<P class="p590 ft113">Article 32 – Trans!border access to stored computer data with consent or where publicly available</P>
<P class="p475 ft90">A Party may, without the authorisation of another Party:</P>
<P class="p514 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">a </SPAN>access publicly available (open source) stored computer data, regardless of where the data is located geographically; or</P>
<P class="p514 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">b </SPAN>access or receive, through a computer system in its territory, stored computer data located in another Party, if the Party obtains the lawful and voluntary consent of the person who has the lawful authority to disclose the data to the Party through that computer system.</P>
</DIV>
<DIV id="id_2">
<P class="p164 ft2">96</P>
</DIV>
</DIV>
<DIV id="page_97">


<DIV id="id_1">
<P class="p452 ft2">Prop. 2020/21:72</P>
<P class="p453 ft2">Bilaga 1</P>
<P class="p454 ft93">ETS 185 – Cybercrime (Convention), 23.XI.2001</P>
<P class="p455 ft93">__________________________________________________________________________________</P>
<P class="p476 ft86">Article 33 – Mutual assistance regarding the real!time collection of traffic data</P>
<P class="p591 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">1</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">The Parties shall provide mutual assistance to each other in the </SPAN><NOBR>real-time</NOBR> collection of traffic data associated with specified communications in their territory transmitted by means of a computer system. Subject to the provisions of paragraph 2, this assistance shall be governed by the conditions and procedures provided for under domestic law.</P>
<P class="p592 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">2</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">Each Party shall provide such assistance at least with respect to criminal offences for which </SPAN><NOBR>real-time</NOBR> collection of traffic data would be available in a similar domestic case.</P>
<P class="p479 ft86">Article 34 – Mutual assistance regarding the interception of content data</P>
<P class="p480 ft90">The Parties shall provide mutual assistance to each other in the <NOBR>real-time</NOBR> collection or recording of content data of specified communications transmitted by means of a computer system to the extent permitted under their applicable treaties and domestic laws.</P>
<P class="p593 ft91">Title 3 – 24/7 Network</P>
<P class="p476 ft86">Article 35 – 24/7 Network</P>
<P class="p591 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">1</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">Each Party shall designate a point of contact available on a </SPAN><NOBR>twenty-four</NOBR> hour, <NOBR>seven-day-a-</NOBR> week basis, in order to ensure the provision of immediate assistance for the purpose of investigations or proceedings concerning criminal offences related to computer systems and data, or for the collection of evidence in electronic form of a criminal offence. Such assistance shall include facilitating, or, if permitted by its domestic law and practice, directly carrying out the following measures:</P>
<P class="p594 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">a </SPAN>the provision of technical advice;</P>
<P class="p476 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">b </SPAN>the preservation of data pursuant to Articles 29 and 30;</P>
<P class="p476 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">c</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">the collection of evidence, the provision of legal information, and locating of suspects.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p595 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">2</SPAN><SPAN class="ft114">a </SPAN>A Party’s point of contact shall have the capacity to carry out communications with the point of contact of another Party on an expedited basis.</P>
<P class="p487 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">b</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">If the point of contact designated by a Party is not part of that Party’s authority or authorities responsible for international mutual assistance or extradition, the point of contact shall ensure that it is able to </SPAN><NOBR>co-ordinate</NOBR> with such authority or authorities on an expedited basis.</P>
<P class="p592 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">3</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">Each Party shall ensure that trained and equipped personnel are available, in order to facilitate the operation of the network.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p596 ft86">Chapter IV – Final provisions</P>
<P class="p597 ft86">Article 36 – Signature and entry into force</P>
<P class="p538 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">1</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">This Convention shall be open for signature by the member States of the Council of Europe and by </SPAN><NOBR>non-member</NOBR> States which have participated in its elaboration.</P>
<P class="p520 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">2</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">This Convention is subject to ratification, acceptance or approval. Instruments of ratification, acceptance or approval shall be deposited with the Secretary General of the Council of Europe.</SPAN></P>
</DIV>
<DIV id="id_2">
<P class="p164 ft2">97</P>
</DIV>
</DIV>
<DIV id="page_98">


<DIV id="id_1">
<P class="p164 ft2">Prop. 2020/21:72</P>
<P class="p440 ft2">Bilaga 1</P>
<P class="p463 ft93">ETS 185 – Cybercrime (Convention), 23.XI.2001</P>
<P class="p464 ft93">__________________________________________________________________________________</P>
<P class="p508 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">3</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">This Convention shall enter into force on the first day of the month following the expiration of a period of three months after the date on which five States, including at least three member States of the Council of Europe, have expressed their consent to be bound by the Convention in accordance with the provisions of paragraphs 1 and 2.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p560 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">4</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">In respect of any signatory State which subsequently expresses its consent to be bound by it, the Convention shall enter into force on the first day of the month following the expiration of a period of three months after the date of the expression of its consent to be bound by the Convention in accordance with the provisions of paragraphs 1 and 2.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p579 ft86">Article 37 – Accession to the Convention</P>
<P class="p508 ft92"><SPAN class="ft94">1</SPAN><SPAN class="ft105">After the entry into force of this Convention, the Committee of Ministers of the Council of Europe, after consulting with and obtaining the unanimous consent of the Contracting States to the Convention, may invite any State which is not a member of the Council and which has not participated in its elaboration to accede to this Convention. The decision shall be taken by the majority provided for in Article 20.d. of the Statute of the Council of Europe and by the unanimous vote of the representatives of the Contracting States entitled to sit on the Committee of Ministers.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p494 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">2</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">In respect of any State acceding to the Convention under paragraph 1 above, the Convention shall enter into force on the first day of the month following the expiration of a period of three months after the date of deposit of the instrument of accession with the Secretary General of the Council of Europe.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p579 ft86">Article 38 – Territorial application</P>
<P class="p494 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">1</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">Any State may, at the time of signature or when depositing its instrument of ratification, acceptance, approval or accession, specify the territory or territories to which this Convention shall apply.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p511 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">2</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">Any State may, at any later date, by a declaration addressed to the Secretary General of the Council of Europe, extend the application of this Convention to any other territory specified in the declaration. In respect of such territory the Convention shall enter into force on the first day of the month following the expiration of a period of three months after the date of receipt of the declaration by the Secretary General.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p543 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">3</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">Any declaration made under the two preceding paragraphs may, in respect of any territory specified in such declaration, be withdrawn by a notification addressed to the Secretary General of the Council of Europe. The withdrawal shall become effective on the first day of the month following the expiration of a period of three months after the date of receipt of such notification by the Secretary General.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p587 ft86">Article 39 – Effects of the Convention</P>
<P class="p526 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">1</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">The purpose of the present Convention is to supplement applicable multilateral or bilateral treaties or arrangements as between the Parties, including the provisions of:</SPAN></P>
<P class="p514 ft90"><SPAN class="ft90">–</SPAN><SPAN class="ft119">the European Convention on Extradition, opened for signature in Paris, on 13 December 1957 (ETS No. 24);</SPAN></P>
<P class="p514 ft90"><SPAN class="ft90">–</SPAN><SPAN class="ft119">the European Convention on Mutual Assistance in Criminal Matters, opened for signature in Strasbourg, on 20 April 1959 (ETS No. 30);</SPAN></P>
<P class="p529 ft90"><SPAN class="ft90">–</SPAN><SPAN class="ft119">the Additional Protocol to the European Convention on Mutual Assistance in Criminal Matters, opened for signature in Strasbourg, on 17 March 1978 (ETS No. 99).</SPAN></P>
</DIV>
<DIV id="id_2">
<P class="p164 ft2">98</P>
</DIV>
</DIV>
<DIV id="page_99">


<DIV id="id_1">
<P class="p452 ft2">Prop. 2020/21:72</P>
<P class="p453 ft2">Bilaga 1</P>
<P class="p454 ft93">ETS 185 – Cybercrime (Convention), 23.XI.2001</P>
<P class="p455 ft93">__________________________________________________________________________________</P>
<P class="p552 ft92"><SPAN class="ft94">2</SPAN><SPAN class="ft105">If two or more Parties have already concluded an agreement or treaty on the matters dealt with in this Convention or have otherwise established their relations on such matters, or should they in future do so, they shall also be entitled to apply that agreement or treaty or to regulate those relations accordingly. However, where Parties establish their relations in respect of the matters dealt with in the present Convention other than as regulated therein, they shall do so in a manner that is not inconsistent with the Convention’s objectives and principles.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p598 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">3</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">Nothing in this Convention shall affect other rights, restrictions, obligations and responsibilities of a Party.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p571 ft86">Article 40 – Declarations</P>
<P class="p480 ft90">By a written notification addressed to the Secretary General of the Council of Europe, any State may, at the time of signature or when depositing its instrument of ratification, acceptance, approval or accession, declare that it avails itself of the possibility of requiring additional elements as provided for under Articles 2, 3, 6 paragraph 1.b, 7, 9 paragraph 3, and 27, paragraph 9.e.</P>
<P class="p537 ft86">Article 41 – Federal clause</P>
<P class="p591 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">1</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">A federal State may reserve the right to assume obligations under Chapter II of this Convention consistent with its fundamental principles governing the relationship between its central government and constituent States or other similar territorial entities provided that it is still able to </SPAN><NOBR>co-operate</NOBR> under Chapter III.</P>
<P class="p559 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">2</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">When making a reservation under paragraph 1, a federal State may not apply the terms of such reservation to exclude or substantially diminish its obligations to provide for measures set forth in Chapter II. Overall, it shall provide for a broad and effective law enforcement capability with respect to those measures.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p559 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">3</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">With regard to the provisions of this Convention, the application of which comes under the jurisdiction of constituent States or other similar territorial entities, that are not obliged by the constitutional system of the federation to take legislative measures, the federal government shall inform the competent authorities of such States of the said provisions with its favourable opinion, encouraging them to take appropriate action to give them effect.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p537 ft86">Article 42 – Reservations</P>
<P class="p480 ft90">By a written notification addressed to the Secretary General of the Council of Europe, any State may, at the time of signature or when depositing its instrument of ratification, acceptance, approval or accession, declare that it avails itself of the reservation(s) provided for in Article 4, paragraph 2, Article 6, paragraph 3, Article 9, paragraph 4, Article 10, paragraph 3, Article 11, paragraph 3, Article 14, paragraph 3, Article 22, paragraph 2, Article 29, paragraph 4, and Article 41, paragraph 1. No other reservation may be made.</P>
<P class="p594 ft86">Article 43 – Status and withdrawal of reservations</P>
<P class="p503 ft104"><SPAN class="ft94">1</SPAN><SPAN class="ft103">A Party that has made a reservation in accordance with Article 42 may wholly or partially withdraw it by means of a notification addressed to the Secretary General of the Council of Europe. Such withdrawal shall take effect on the date of receipt of such notification by the Secretary General. If the notification states that the withdrawal of a reservation is to take effect on a date specified therein, and such date is later than the date on which the notification is received by the Secretary General, the withdrawal shall take effect on such a later date.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p599 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">2</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">A Party that has made a reservation as referred to in Article 42 shall withdraw such reservation, in whole or in part, as soon as circumstances so permit.</SPAN></P>
</DIV>
<DIV id="id_2">
<P class="p164 ft2">99</P>
</DIV>
</DIV>
<DIV id="page_100">


<DIV id="id_1">
<P class="p164 ft2">Prop. 2020/21:72</P>
<P class="p440 ft2">Bilaga 1</P>
<P class="p463 ft93">ETS 185 – Cybercrime (Convention), 23.XI.2001</P>
<P class="p464 ft93">__________________________________________________________________________________</P>
<P class="p508 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">3</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">The Secretary General of the Council of Europe may periodically enquire with Parties that have made one or more reservations as referred to in Article 42 as to the prospects for withdrawing such reservation(s).</SPAN></P>
<P class="p549 ft86">Article 44 – Amendments</P>
<P class="p494 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">1</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">Amendments to this Convention may be proposed by any Party, and shall be communicated by the Secretary General of the Council of Europe to the member States of the Council of Europe, to the </SPAN><NOBR>non-member</NOBR> States which have participated in the elaboration of this Convention as well as to any State which has acceded to, or has been invited to accede to, this Convention in accordance with the provisions of Article 37.</P>
<P class="p543 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">2</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">Any amendment proposed by a Party shall be communicated to the European Committee on Crime Problems (CDPC), which shall submit to the Committee of Ministers its opinion on that proposed amendment.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p546 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">3</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">The Committee of Ministers shall consider the proposed amendment and the opinion submitted by the CDPC and, following consultation with the </SPAN><NOBR>non-member</NOBR> States Parties to this Convention, may adopt the amendment.</P>
<P class="p564 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">4</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">The text of any amendment adopted by the Committee of Ministers in accordance with paragraph 3 of this article shall be forwarded to the Parties for acceptance.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p565 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">5</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">Any amendment adopted in accordance with paragraph 3 of this article shall come into force on the thirtieth day after all Parties have informed the Secretary General of their acceptance thereof.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p549 ft86">Article 45 – Settlement of disputes</P>
<P class="p526 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">1</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">The European Committee on Crime Problems (CDPC) shall be kept informed regarding the interpretation and application of this Convention.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p565 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">2</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">In case of a dispute between Parties as to the interpretation or application of this Convention, they shall seek a settlement of the dispute through negotiation or any other peaceful means of their choice, including submission of the dispute to the CDPC, to an arbitral tribunal whose decisions shall be binding upon the Parties, or to the International Court of Justice, as agreed upon by the Parties concerned.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p587 ft86">Article 46 – Consultations of the Parties</P>
<P class="p472 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">1</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">The Parties shall, as appropriate, consult periodically with a view to facilitating:</SPAN></P>
<P class="p465 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">a </SPAN>the effective use and implementation of this Convention, including the identification of any problems thereof, as well as the effects of any declaration or reservation made under this Convention;</P>
<P class="p495 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">b </SPAN>the exchange of information on significant legal, policy or technological developments pertaining to cybercrime and the collection of evidence in electronic form;</P>
<P class="p500 ft90"><SPAN class="ft96">c</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">consideration of possible supplementation or amendment of the Convention.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p600 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">2</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">The European Committee on Crime Problems (CDPC) shall be kept periodically informed regarding the result of consultations referred to in paragraph 1.</SPAN></P>
</DIV>
<DIV id="id_2">
<P class="p164 ft2">100</P>
</DIV>
</DIV>
<DIV id="page_101">


<DIV id="id_1">
<P class="p452 ft2">Prop. 2020/21:72</P>
<P class="p453 ft2">Bilaga 1</P>
<P class="p454 ft93">ETS 185 – Cybercrime (Convention), 23.XI.2001</P>
<P class="p455 ft93">__________________________________________________________________________________</P>
<P class="p501 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">3</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">The CDPC shall, as appropriate, facilitate the consultations referred to in paragraph 1 and take the measures necessary to assist the Parties in their efforts to supplement or amend the Convention. At the latest three years after the present Convention enters into force, the European Committee on Crime Problems (CDPC) shall, in </SPAN><NOBR>co-operation</NOBR> with the Parties, conduct a review of all of the Convention’s provisions and, if necessary, recommend any appropriate amendments.</P>
<P class="p524 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">4</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">Except where assumed by the Council of Europe, expenses incurred in carrying out the provisions of paragraph 1 shall be borne by the Parties in the manner to be determined by them.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p478 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">5</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">The Parties shall be assisted by the Secretariat of the Council of Europe in carrying out their functions pursuant to this article.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p479 ft86">Article 47 – Denunciation</P>
<P class="p538 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">1</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">Any Party may, at any time, denounce this Convention by means of a notification addressed to the Secretary General of the Council of Europe.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p520 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">2</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">Such denunciation shall become effective on the first day of the month following the expiration of a period of three months after the date of receipt of the notification by the Secretary General.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p571 ft86">Article 48 – Notification</P>
<P class="p480 ft90">The Secretary General of the Council of Europe shall notify the member States of the Council of Europe, the <NOBR>non-member</NOBR> States which have participated in the elaboration of this Convention as well as any State which has acceded to, or has been invited to accede to, this Convention of:</P>
<P class="p481 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">a </SPAN>any signature;</P>
<P class="p476 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">b </SPAN>the deposit of any instrument of ratification, acceptance, approval or accession;</P>
<P class="p476 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">c </SPAN>any date of entry into force of this Convention in accordance with Articles 36 and 37;</P>
<P class="p601 ft112"><SPAN class="ft118">d </SPAN>any declaration made under Article 40 or reservation made in accordance with Article 42; <SPAN class="ft118">e </SPAN>any other act, notification or communication relating to this Convention.</P>
<P class="p602 ft90">In witness whereof the undersigned, being duly authorised thereto, have signed this Convention.</P>
<P class="p603 ft90">Done at Budapest, this 23rd day of November 2001, in English and in French, both texts being equally authentic, in a single copy which shall be deposited in the archives of the Council of Europe. The Secretary General of the Council of Europe shall transmit certified copies to each member State of the Council of Europe, to the <NOBR>non-member</NOBR> States which have participated in the elaboration of this Convention, and to any State invited to accede to it.</P>
</DIV>
<DIV id="id_2">
<P class="p164 ft2">101</P>
</DIV>
</DIV>
<DIV id="page_102">
<DIV id="p102dimg1">
<INGENBILD zsrc="H80372102x1.jpg/" id="p102img1">
</DIV>


<DIV id="id_1">
<P class="p164 ft2">Prop. 2020/21:72</P>
<P class="p440 ft2">Bilaga 1</P>
<P class="p441 ft87">European Treaty Series <SPAN class="ft86">! </SPAN>No. 189</P>
<P class="p604 ft88">Additional Protocol to the Convention on Cybercrime, concerning the criminalisation of acts of a racist and xenophobic nature committed through computer systems</P>
<P class="p605 ft89">Strasbourg, 28.I.2003</P>
<P class="p606 ft90">The member States of the Council of Europe and the other States Parties to the Convention on Cybercrime, opened for signature in Budapest on 23 November 2001, signatory hereto;</P>
<P class="p447 ft90">Considering that the aim of the Council of Europe is to achieve a greater unity between its members;</P>
<P class="p500 ft90">Recalling that all human beings are born free and equal in dignity and rights;</P>
<P class="p447 ft90">Stressing the need to secure a full and effective implementation of all human rights without any discrimination or distinction, as enshrined in European and other international instruments;</P>
<P class="p450 ft90">Convinced that acts of a racist and xenophobic nature constitute a violation of human rights and a threat to the rule of law and democratic stability;</P>
<P class="p447 ft90">Considering that national and international law need to provide adequate legal responses to propaganda of a racist and xenophobic nature committed through computer systems;</P>
<P class="p450 ft90">Aware of the fact that propaganda to such acts is often subject to criminalisation in national legislation;</P>
<P class="p447 ft90">Having regard to the Convention on Cybercrime, which provides for modern and flexible means of international <NOBR>co-operation</NOBR> and convinced of the need to harmonise substantive law provisions concerning the fight against racist and xenophobic propaganda;</P>
<P class="p451 ft90">Aware that computer systems offer an unprecedented means of facilitating freedom of expression and communication around the globe;</P>
<P class="p447 ft90">Recognising that freedom of expression constitutes one of the essential foundations of a democratic society, and is one of the basic conditions for its progress and for the development of every human being;</P>
<P class="p451 ft90">Concerned, however, by the risk of misuse or abuse of such computer systems to disseminate racist and xenophobic propaganda;</P>
<P class="p447 ft90">Mindful of the need to ensure a proper balance between freedom of expression and an effective fight against acts of a racist and xenophobic nature;</P>
<P class="p607 ft90">Recognising that this Protocol is not intended to affect established principles relating to freedom of expression in national legal systems;</P>
</DIV>
<DIV id="id_2">
<P class="p164 ft2">102</P>
</DIV>
</DIV>
<DIV id="page_103">


<DIV id="id_1">
<P class="p452 ft2">Prop. 2020/21:72</P>
<P class="p453 ft2">Bilaga 1</P>
<P class="p608 ft93">ETS 189 – Cybercrime (Additional Protocol), 28.I.2003</P>
<P class="p455 ft93">__________________________________________________________________________________</P>
<P class="p609 ft92">Taking into account the relevant international legal instruments in this field, and in particular the Convention for the Protection of Human Rights and Fundamental Freedoms and its Protocol No. 12 concerning the general prohibition of discrimination, the existing Council of Europe conventions on <NOBR>co-operation</NOBR> in the penal field, in particular the Convention on Cybercrime, the United Nations International Convention on the Elimination of All Forms of Racial Discrimination of 21 December 1965, the European Union Joint Action of 15 July 1996 adopted by the Council on the basis of Article K.3 of the Treaty on European Union, concerning action to combat racism and xenophobia;</P>
<P class="p457 ft90">Welcoming the recent developments which further advance international understanding and <NOBR>co-operation</NOBR> in combating cybercrime and racism and xenophobia;</P>
<P class="p610 ft90">Having regard to the Action Plan adopted by the Heads of State and Government of the Council of Europe on the occasion of their Second Summit (Strasbourg, <NOBR>10-11</NOBR> October 1997) to seek common responses to the developments of the new technologies based on the standards and values of the Council of Europe;</P>
<P class="p481 ft90">Have agreed as follows:</P>
<P class="p611 ft86">Chapter I – Common provisions</P>
<P class="p597 ft86">Article 1 – Purpose</P>
<P class="p480 ft90">The purpose of this Protocol is to supplement, as between the Parties to the Protocol, the provisions of the Convention on Cybercrime, opened for signature in Budapest on 23 November 2001 (hereinafter referred to as “the Convention”), as regards the criminalisation of acts of a racist and xenophobic nature committed through computer systems.</P>
<P class="p612 ft86">Article 2 – Definition</P>
<P class="p613 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">1</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">For the purposes of this Protocol:</SPAN></P>
<P class="p610 ft90">"<SPAN class="ft91">racist and xenophobic material</SPAN>" means any written material, any image or any other representation of ideas or theories, which advocates, promotes or incites hatred, discrimination or violence, against any individual or group of individuals, based on race, colour, descent or national or ethnic origin, as well as religion if used as a pretext for any of these factors.</P>
<P class="p592 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">2</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">The terms and expressions used in this Protocol shall be interpreted in the same manner as they are interpreted under the Convention.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p614 ft86">Chapter II – Measures to be taken at national level</P>
<P class="p597 ft86">Article 3 – Dissemination of racist and xenophobic material through computer systems</P>
<P class="p477 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">1</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">Each Party shall adopt such legislative and other measures as may be necessary to establish as criminal offences under its domestic law, when committed intentionally and without right, the following conduct:</SPAN></P>
<P class="p615 ft90">distributing, or otherwise making available, racist and xenophobic material to the public through a computer system.</P>
<P class="p520 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">2</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">A Party may reserve the right not to attach criminal liability to conduct as defined by paragraph 1 of this article, where the material, as defined in Article 2, paragraph 1, advocates, promotes or incites discrimination that is not associated with hatred or violence, provided that other effective remedies are available.</SPAN></P>
</DIV>
<DIV id="id_2">
<P class="p164 ft2">103</P>
</DIV>
</DIV>
<DIV id="page_104">


<DIV id="id_1">
<P class="p164 ft2">Prop. 2020/21:72</P>
<P class="p440 ft2">Bilaga 1</P>
<P class="p616 ft93">ETS 189 – Cybercrime (Additional Protocol), 28.I.2003</P>
<P class="p464 ft93">__________________________________________________________________________________</P>
<P class="p508 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">3</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">Notwithstanding paragraph 2 of this article, a Party may reserve the right not to apply paragraph 1 to those cases of discrimination for which, due to established principles in its national legal system concerning freedom of expression, it cannot provide for effective remedies as referred to in the said paragraph 2.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p579 ft86">Article 4 – Racist and xenophobic motivated threat</P>
<P class="p494 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">1</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">Each Party shall adopt such legislative and other measures as may be necessary to establish as criminal offences under its domestic law, when committed intentionally and without right, the following conduct:</SPAN></P>
<P class="p450 ft90">threatening, through a computer system, with the commission of a serious criminal offence as defined under its domestic law, (i) persons for the reason that they belong to a group, distinguished by race, colour, descent or national or ethnic origin, as well as religion, if used as a pretext for any of these factors, or (ii) a group of persons which is distinguished by any of these characteristics.</P>
<P class="p587 ft86">Article 5 – Racist and xenophobic motivated insult</P>
<P class="p508 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">1</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">Each Party shall adopt such legislative and other measures as may be necessary to establish as criminal offences under its domestic law, when committed intentionally and without right, the following conduct:</SPAN></P>
<P class="p450 ft90">insulting publicly, through a computer system, (i) persons for the reason that they belong to a group distinguished by race, colour, descent or national or ethnic origin, as well as religion, if used as a pretext for any of these factors; or (ii) a group of persons which is distinguished by any of these characteristics.</P>
<P class="p617 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">2</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">A Party may either:</SPAN></P>
<P class="p465 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">a </SPAN>require that the offence referred to in paragraph 1 of this article has the effect that the person or group of persons referred to in paragraph 1 is exposed to hatred, contempt or ridicule; or</P>
<P class="p467 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">b </SPAN>reserve the right not to apply, in whole or in part, paragraph 1 of this article.</P>
<P class="p618 ft113">Article 6 – Denial, gross minimisation, approval or justification of genocide or crimes against humanity</P>
<P class="p565 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">1</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">Each Party shall adopt such legislative measures as may be necessary to establish the following conduct as criminal offences under its domestic law, when committed intentionally and without right:</SPAN></P>
<P class="p451 ft90">distributing or otherwise making available, through a computer system to the public, material which denies, grossly minimises, approves or justifies acts constituting genocide or crimes against humanity, as defined by international law and recognised as such by final and binding decisions of the International Military Tribunal, established by the London Agreement of 8 August 1945, or of any other international court established by relevant international instruments and whose jurisdiction is recognised by that Party.</P>
<P class="p588 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">2</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">A Party may either</SPAN></P>
<P class="p465 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">a </SPAN>require that the denial or the gross minimisation referred to in paragraph 1 of this article is committed with the intent to incite hatred, discrimination or violence against any individual or group of individuals, based on race, colour, descent or national or ethnic origin, as well as religion if used as a pretext for any of these factors, or otherwise</P>
</DIV>
<DIV id="id_2">
<P class="p164 ft2">104</P>
</DIV>
</DIV>
<DIV id="page_105">


<DIV id="id_1">
<P class="p452 ft2">Prop. 2020/21:72</P>
<P class="p453 ft2">Bilaga 1</P>
<P class="p608 ft93">ETS 189 – Cybercrime (Additional Protocol), 28.I.2003</P>
<P class="p455 ft93">__________________________________________________________________________________</P>
<P class="p476 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">b</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">reserve the right not to apply, in whole or in part, paragraph 1 of this article.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p476 ft86">Article 7 – Aiding and abetting</P>
<P class="p480 ft90">Each Party shall adopt such legislative and other measures as may be necessary to establish as criminal offences under its domestic law, when committed intentionally and without right, aiding or abetting the commission of any of the offences established in accordance with this Protocol, with intent that such offence be committed.</P>
<P class="p619 ft86">Chapter III – Relations between the Convention and this Protocol</P>
<P class="p597 ft86">Article 8 – Relations between the Convention and this Protocol</P>
<P class="p620 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">1</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">Articles 1, 12, 13, 22, 41, 44, 45 and 46 of the Convention shall apply, </SPAN><SPAN class="ft91">mutatis mutandis</SPAN>, to this Protocol.</P>
<P class="p575 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">2</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">The Parties shall extend the scope of application of the measures defined in Articles 14 to 21 and Articles 23 to 35 of the Convention, to Articles 2 to 7 of this Protocol.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p621 ft86">Chapter IV – Final provisions</P>
<P class="p597 ft86">Article 9 – Expression of consent to be bound</P>
<P class="p538 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">1</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">This Protocol shall be open for signature by the States which have signed the Convention, which may express their consent to be bound by either:</SPAN></P>
<P class="p479 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">a </SPAN>signature without reservation as to ratification, acceptance or approval; or</P>
<P class="p550 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">b</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">subject to ratification, acceptance or approval, followed by ratification, acceptance or approval.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p520 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">2</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">A State may not sign this Protocol without reservation as to ratification, acceptance or approval, or deposit an instrument of ratification, acceptance or approval, unless it has already deposited or simultaneously deposits an instrument of ratification, acceptance or approval of the Convention.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p592 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">3</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">The instruments of ratification, acceptance or approval shall be deposited with the Secretary General of the Council of Europe.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p479 ft86">Article 10 – Entry into force</P>
<P class="p591 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">1</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">This Protocol shall enter into force on the first day of the month following the expiration of a period of three months after the date on which five States have expressed their consent to be bound by the Protocol, in accordance with the provisions of Article 9.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p572 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">2</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">In respect of any State which subsequently expresses its consent to be bound by it, the Protocol shall enter into force on the first day of the month following the expiration of a period of three months after the date of its signature without reservation as to ratification, acceptance or approval or deposit of its instrument of ratification, acceptance or approval.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p481 ft86">Article 11 – Accession</P>
<P class="p538 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">1</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">After the entry into force of this Protocol, any State which has acceded to the Convention may also accede to the Protocol.</SPAN></P>
</DIV>
<DIV id="id_2">
<P class="p164 ft2">105</P>
</DIV>
</DIV>
<DIV id="page_106">


<DIV id="id_1">
<P class="p164 ft2">Prop. 2020/21:72</P>
<P class="p440 ft2">Bilaga 1</P>
<P class="p616 ft93">ETS 189 – Cybercrime (Additional Protocol), 28.I.2003</P>
<P class="p464 ft93">__________________________________________________________________________________</P>
<P class="p508 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">2</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">Accession shall be effected by the deposit with the Secretary General of the Council of Europe of an instrument of accession which shall take effect on the first day of the month following the expiration of a period of three months after the date of its deposit.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p549 ft86">Article 12 – Reservations and declarations</P>
<P class="p494 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">1</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">Reservations and declarations made by a Party to a provision of the Convention shall be applicable also to this Protocol, unless that Party declares otherwise at the time of signature or when depositing its instrument of ratification, acceptance, approval or accession.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p543 ft92"><SPAN class="ft94">2</SPAN><SPAN class="ft105">By a written notification addressed to the Secretary General of the Council of Europe, any Party may, at the time of signature or when depositing its instrument of ratification, acceptance, approval or accession, declare that it avails itself of the reservation(s) provided for in Articles 3, 5 and 6 of this Protocol. At the same time, a Party may avail itself, with respect to the provisions of this Protocol, of the reservation(s) provided for in Article 22, paragraph 2, and Article 41, paragraph 1, of the Convention, irrespective of the implementation made by that Party under the Convention. No other reservations may be made.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p548 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">3</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">By a written notification addressed to the Secretary General of the Council of Europe, any State may, at the time of signature or when depositing its instrument of ratification, acceptance, approval or accession, declare that it avails itself of the possibility of requiring additional elements as provided for in Article 5, paragraph 2.a, and Article 6, paragraph 2.a, of this Protocol.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p587 ft86">Article 13 – Status and withdrawal of reservations</P>
<P class="p622 ft104"><SPAN class="ft94">1</SPAN><SPAN class="ft103">A Party that has made a reservation in accordance with Article 12 above shall withdraw such reservation, in whole or in part, as soon as circumstances so permit. Such withdrawal shall take effect on the date of receipt of a notification addressed to the Secretary General of the Council of Europe. If the notification states that the withdrawal of a reservation is to take effect on a date specified therein, and such date is later than the date on which the notification is received by the Secretary General, the withdrawal shall take effect on such a later date.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p623 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">2</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">The Secretary General of the Council of Europe may periodically enquire with Parties that have made one or more reservations in accordance with Article 12 as to the prospects for withdrawing such reservation(s).</SPAN></P>
<P class="p549 ft86">Article 14 – Territorial application</P>
<P class="p494 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">1</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">Any Party may at the time of signature or when depositing its instrument of ratification, acceptance, approval or accession, specify the territory or territories to which this Protocol shall apply.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p546 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">2</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">Any Party may, at any later date, by a declaration addressed to the Secretary General of the Council of Europe, extend the application of this Protocol to any other territory specified in the declaration. In respect of such territory, the Protocol shall enter into force on the first day of the month following the expiration of a period of three months after the date of receipt of the declaration by the Secretary General.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p543 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">3</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">Any declaration made under the two preceding paragraphs may, in respect of any territory specified in such declaration, be withdrawn by a notification addressed to the Secretary General of the Council of Europe. The withdrawal shall become effective on the first day of the month following the expiration of a period of three months after the date of receipt of such notification by the Secretary General.</SPAN></P>
</DIV>

<P class="p455 ft93">__________________________________________________________________________________</P>
<P class="p476 ft86">Article 15 – Denunciation</P>
<P class="p538 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">1</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">Any Party may, at any time, denounce this Protocol by means of a notification addressed to the Secretary General of the Council of Europe.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p535 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">2</SPAN><SPAN class="ft97">Such denunciation shall become effective on the first day of the month following the expiration of a period of three months after the date of receipt of the notification by the Secretary General.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p462 ft86">Article 16 – Notification</P>
<P class="p624 ft90">The Secretary General of the Council of Europe shall notify the member States of the Council of Europe, the <NOBR>non-member</NOBR> States which have participated in the elaboration of this Protocol as well as any State which has acceded to, or has been invited to accede to, this Protocol of:</P>
<P class="p571 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">a </SPAN>any signature;</P>
<P class="p479 ft90"><SPAN class="ft94">b </SPAN>the deposit of any instrument of ratification, acceptance, approval or accession;</P>
<P class="p625 ft102"><SPAN class="ft101">c </SPAN>any date of entry into force of this Protocol in accordance with its Articles 9, 10 and 11; <SPAN class="ft101">d </SPAN>any other act, notification or communication relating to this Protocol.</P>
<P class="p626 ft90">In witness whereof the undersigned, being duly authorised thereto, have signed this Protocol.</P>
<P class="p627 ft90">Done at Strasbourg, this 28th day of January 2003, in English and in French, both texts being equally authentic, in a single copy which shall be deposited in the archives of the Council of Europe. The Secretary General of the Council of Europe shall transmit certified copies to each member State of the Council of Europe, to the <NOBR>non-member</NOBR> States which have participated in the elaboration of this Protocol, and to any State invited to accede to it.</P>

<DIV id="id_1_2">
<P class="p164 ft55">Europarådets konvention om <NOBR>it-relaterad</NOBR> brottslighet (ETS 185) och tilläggsprotokollet (ETS 189)</P>
</DIV>
</DIV>
<DIV id="id_2">
<P class="p628 ft12">Europarådets konvention om <NOBR>it-relaterad</NOBR> brottslighet (ETS 185)</P>
<P class="p629 ft120">(Inofficiell översättning)</P>
<P class="p630 ft120">Budapest den 23 november 2001</P>
<P class="p631 ft120">Medlemsstaterna i Europarådet och de övriga stater som har undertecknat denna konvention,</P>
<P class="p632 ft120">som beaktar att Europarådets syfte är att skapa en fastare enhet mellan dess medlemmar,</P>
<P class="p631 ft120">som erkänner värdet av att främja samarbete med de övriga stater som är parter i denna konvention,</P>
<P class="p633 ft121">som är övertygade om nödvändigheten av att, som en prioriterad fråga, driva en gemensam straffrättslig politik som syftar till att skydda samhället mot <NOBR>IT-relaterad</NOBR> brottslighet, bl.a. genom att anta lämplig lagstiftning och främja internationellt samarbete,</P>
<P class="p634 ft120">som är medvetna om de djupgående förändringar som har föranletts av digitalisering, konvergens och fortgående globalisering av datornät,</P>
<P class="p633 ft121">som är oroade över faran för att datornät och elektroniska uppgifter också kan användas för att begå brott och att bevisning om sådana brott kan lagras och överföras genom dessa datornät,</P>
<P class="p635 ft120">som erkänner behovet av samarbete mellan staterna och det privata näringslivet i att bekämpa <NOBR>IT-relaterad</NOBR> brottslighet och behovet av att skydda rättmätiga intressen beträffande användning och utveckling av informationsteknologier,</P>
<P class="p632 ft122">som anser att en effektiv kamp mot <NOBR>IT-relaterad</NOBR> brottslighet fordrar ett utvidgat, snabbt och väl fungerande internationellt samarbete i straffrättsliga frågor,</P>
<P class="p636 ft2">108</P>
</DIV>
</DIV>
<DIV id="page_109">


<DIV>
<DIV id="id_1">
<P class="p223 ft123">som är övertygade om att denna konvention behövs för att avskräcka från gärningar som riktar sig mot datorsystemens, datornätens och de datorbehandlingsbara uppgifternas förtrolighet, integritet och tillgänglighet, liksom från missbruk av dessa system, nät och uppgifter genom att föreskriva att sådana gärningar kriminaliseras så som det beskrivs i konventionen, och att befogenheter som är tillräckliga för att effektivt bekämpa dessa brott införs, genom att underlätta upptäckt, utredning och lagföring av dem, både på det nationella och det internationella planet och genom att sörja för system för ett snabbt och pålitligt internationellt samarbete,</P>
<P class="p637 ft124">som är medvetna om behovet av att säkerställa en lämplig avvägning mellan intresset av att lag och ordning upprätthålls och respekten för de grundläggande mänskliga rättigheterna så som de garanteras i 1950 års Europarådskonvention om skydd för de mänskliga rättigheterna och de grundläggande friheterna, 1966 års <NOBR>FN-konvention</NOBR> om medborgerliga och politiska rättigheter och andra tillämpliga internationella fördrag om mänskliga rättigheter, som bekräftar allas rätt att utan inblandning hysa åsikter liksom rätten till yttrandefrihet, innefattande frihet att söka, ta emot och sprida information och idéer av alla slag, oberoende av gränser, samt rätten till respekt för privatlivet,</P>
<P class="p638 ft120">som också är medvetna om rätten till skydd för personuppgifter, såsom denna rätt tillgodoses exempelvis i 1981 års Europarådskonvention om skydd för enskilda vid automatisk databehandling av personuppgifter,</P>
<P class="p639 ft121">som beaktar 1989 års <NOBR>FN-konvention</NOBR> om barnets rättigheter och 1999 års <NOBR>ILO-konvention</NOBR> mot de värsta formerna av barnarbete,</P>
<P class="p640 ft125">som beaktar de Europarådskonventioner som finns om samarbete på det straffrättsliga området liksom liknande fördrag mellan Europarådets medlemsstater och andra stater och som understryker att den nu aktuella konventionen är avsedd att komplettera dessa konventioner för att effektivisera brottsutredningar och rättegångar om brott relaterade till datorsystem och datorbehandlingsbara uppgifter samt möjliggöra insamling av bevis i elektronisk form om brott,</P>
<P class="p641 ft120">som välkomnar den senaste utvecklingen som ytterligare främjar internationell förståelse och internationellt samarbete i att bekämpa <NOBR>IT-relaterad</NOBR> brottslighet, innefattande åtgärder</P>
</DIV>
<DIV id="id_2">
<P class="p642 ft2">Prop. 2020/21:72 Bilaga 2</P>
<P class="p643 ft2">109</P>
</DIV>
</DIV>
</DIV>
<DIV id="page_110">


<DIV id="id_1">
<DIV id="id_1_1">
<P class="p164 ft2">Prop. 2020/21:72 Bilaga 2</P>
</DIV>
<DIV id="id_1_2">
<P class="p316 ft120">vidtagna av Förenta nationerna, OECD, Europeiska unionen och G8,</P>
<P class="p644 ft120">som erinrar om ministerkommitténs rekommendationer nr R (85)10 om praktisk tillämpning av Europeiska konventionen om inbördes rättshjälp i brottmål avseende bevisinsamling vid avlyssning av teleförbindelser, nr R (88)2 om piratverksamhet avseende upphovsrätt och närstående rättigheter, nr R (87)15, som reglerar användningen av personuppgifter i polisiär verksamhet, nr R (95)4 om skydd för personuppgifter inom telekommunikationstjänster med särskild hänvisning till telefoni samt nr R (89)9 om datorrelaterade brott, som ger riktlinjer för nationella lagstiftande församlingar om definition av vissa datorbrott och nr R (95)13 om problem inom</P>
<P class="p194 ft120">straffprocessrätten som hör samman med informationsteknologi,</P>
<P class="p645 ft120">som beaktar resolution nr 1, antagen av de europeiska justitieministrarna vid deras tjugoförsta konferens i Prag den <NOBR>10–11</NOBR> juni 1997, vilken rekommenderar ministerkommittén att stödja det arbete om <NOBR>IT-brottslighet</NOBR> som utförs av Europarådets kommitté för brottsfrågor för att tillnärma olika länders nationella straffrättsliga bestämmelser och möjliggöra användning av effektiva utredningsmetoder i fråga om sådana brott, liksom resolution nr 3, antagen vid de europeiska justitieministrarnas tjugotredje konferens i London den <NOBR>8–9</NOBR> juni 2000, vilken uppmanar de förhandlande parterna att fortsätta sina ansträngningar med sikte på att finna lämpliga lösningar för att göra det möjligt för största möjliga antal stater att bli parter i konventionen och erkänner behovet av ett snabbt och effektivt system för internationellt samarbete, vari vederbörligen beaktas de särskilda krav som ställs i kampen mot <NOBR>IT-relaterad</NOBR> brottslighet,</P>
<P class="p646 ft121">som även beaktar den handlingsplan som antogs av Europarådets stats- och regeringschefer vid deras andra toppmöte i Strasbourg den <NOBR>10–11</NOBR> oktober 1997 för att söka gemensamma svar på utvecklingen av nya informationsteknologier, som grundar sig på Europarådets normer och värderingar,</P>
<P class="p647 ft120">har kommit överens om följande.</P>

<DIV id="id_2">
<P class="p164 ft2">110</P>
</DIV>
</DIV>
<DIV id="page_111">


<DIV id="id_1">
<DIV id="id_1_1">
<P class="p164 ft126">Kapitel I – Användning av termer</P>
<P class="p259 ft127">Artikel 1 – Definitioner</P>
<P class="p402 ft120">I denna konvention används följande definitioner:</P>
<P class="p648 ft120"><SPAN class="ft128">a)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft129">datorsystem</SPAN>: en apparat eller en grupp av sammankopplade apparater eller apparater som hör samman med varandra, av vilka en eller flera genom ett program utför automatiserad behandling av uppgifter.</P>
<P class="p649 ft127"><SPAN class="ft120">b)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft130">datorbehandlingsbara uppgifter</SPAN><SPAN class="ft120">: framställning av fakta, information eller begrepp i en form som lämpar sig för behandling i ett datorsystem, inklusive program som utformats för att få ett datorsystem att utföra en viss funktion.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p220 ft127"><SPAN class="ft131">c)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft132">tjänsteleverantör</SPAN><SPAN class="ft120">:</SPAN></P>
<P class="p648 ft122"><SPAN class="ft120">i)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft133">en offentlig eller privat enhet som erbjuder användarna av dess tjänster möjlighet att kommunicera med hjälp av ett datorsystem, och</SPAN></P>
<P class="p40 ft120"><SPAN class="ft120">ii)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft134">varje annan enhet som behandlar eller lagrar</SPAN></P>
<P class="p650 ft125">datorbehandlingsbara uppgifter för en sådan kommunikationstjänst eller för användarna av en sådan tjänst.</P>
<P class="p651 ft124"><SPAN class="ft120">d)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft135">trafikuppgifter</SPAN>: datorbehandlingsbara uppgifter som hänför sig till ett meddelande som förmedlas med hjälp av ett datorsystem, vilka alstrats av ett datorsystem som ingick i kommunikationskedjan och anger meddelandets ursprung, destination, färdväg, tid, datum, storlek, varaktighet eller typ av underliggande tjänst.</P>
</DIV>
<DIV id="id_1_2">
<P class="p164 ft2">Prop. 2020/21:72 Bilaga 2</P>
</DIV>
</DIV>
<DIV id="id_2">
<P class="p282 ft126">Kapitel II – Åtgärder som ska vidtas på nationell nivå</P>
<P class="p426 ft126">Avsnitt 1 – Materiell straffrätt</P>
<P class="p652 ft136">Avdelning 1 – Brott mot datorbehandlingsbara uppgifters och datorsystems förtrolighet, integritet och tillgänglighet</P>
<P class="p372 ft127">Artikel 2 – Olagligt intrång</P>
<P class="p653 ft121">Varje part ska vidta nödvändiga lagstiftningsåtgärder och andra åtgärder för att i sin nationella lagstiftning straffbelägga orättmätigt intrång i hela eller en del av ett datorsystem, när det görs uppsåtligen. En part får uppställa krav på att brottet begås</P>
<P class="p286 ft2">111</P>
</DIV>
</DIV>
<DIV id="page_112">


<DIV id="id_1">
<DIV id="id_1_1">
<P class="p164 ft2">Prop. 2020/21:72 Bilaga 2</P>
</DIV>
<DIV id="id_1_2">
<P class="p316 ft120">genom intrång i säkerhetsåtgärder med uppsåt att komma över datorbehandlingsbara uppgifter eller med annat brottsligt uppsåt eller mot ett datorsystem som är kopplat till ett annat datorsystem.</P>
<P class="p654 ft127">Artikel 3 – Olaglig avlyssning</P>
<P class="p655 ft121">Varje part ska vidta nödvändiga lagstiftningsåtgärder och andra åtgärder för att i sin nationella lagstiftning straffbelägga följande gärningar när de begås uppsåtligen: att med tekniska hjälpmedel orättmätigt avlyssna icke allmänna överföringar av datorbehandlingsbara uppgifter till, från eller inom ett datorsystem, däribland elektromagnetiska emissioner från ett datorsystem med sådana datorbehandlingsbara uppgifter. En part får uppställa krav på att brottet begås med brottsligt uppsåt eller mot ett datorsystem som är kopplat till ett annat datorsystem.</P>
<P class="p656 ft127">Artikel 4 – Datastörning</P>
<P class="p657 ft122"><SPAN class="ft128">1.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft137">Varje part ska vidta nödvändiga lagstiftningsåtgärder och andra åtgärder för att i sin nationella lagstiftning straffbelägga följande gärningar när de begås uppsåtligen:</SPAN></P>
<P class="p658 ft120">Att orättmätigt skada, radera, försämra, ändra eller undertrycka datorbehandlingsbara uppgifter.</P>
<P class="p659 ft120"><SPAN class="ft128">2.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft138">En part får förbehålla sig rätten att uppställa krav på att det handlande som anges i punkt 1 medför allvarlig skada.</SPAN></P>
<P class="p120 ft127">Artikel 5 – Systemstörning</P>
<P class="p660 ft120">Varje part ska vidta nödvändiga lagstiftningsåtgärder och andra åtgärder för att i sin nationella lagstiftning straffbelägga följande gärningar när de begås uppsåtligen: att orättmätigt allvarligt hindra ett datorsystems drift genom att mata in, överföra, skada, radera, försämra, ändra eller undertrycka datorbehandlingsbara uppgifter.</P>
</DIV>
</DIV>
<DIV id="id_2">
<P class="p164 ft2">112</P>
</DIV>
</DIV>
<DIV id="page_113">


<DIV id="id_1">
<DIV id="id_1_1">
<P class="p164 ft127">Artikel 6 – Missbruk av apparatur</P>
<P class="p661 ft122"><SPAN class="ft128">1.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft137">Varje part ska vidta nödvändiga lagstiftningsåtgärder och andra åtgärder för att i sin nationella lagstiftning straffbelägga följande gärningar när de begås uppsåtligen och orättmätigt:</SPAN></P>
<P class="p662 ft120"><SPAN class="ft128">a)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft139">Att tillverka, försälja, anskaffa för användning, importera, sprida eller på annat sätt tillgängliggöra</SPAN></P>
<P class="p663 ft120"><SPAN class="ft120">i)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft140">en apparat vari ingår ett datorprogram som är skapat eller anpassat främst för att begå något av de brott som straffbeläggs i enlighet med artiklarna </SPAN><NOBR>2–5,</NOBR></P>
<P class="p663 ft120"><SPAN class="ft120">ii)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft141">ett datorlösenord, en åtkomstkod eller liknande datorbehandlingsbara uppgifter som kan ge åtkomst till ett helt datorsystem eller en del därav med uppsåt att den eller det ska användas för att begå något av de brott som straffbeläggs i enlighet med artiklarna </SPAN><NOBR>2–5.</NOBR></P>
<P class="p649 ft120"><SPAN class="ft120">b)</SPAN><SPAN class="ft141">Att inneha ett föremål som avses i a i eller a ii ovan med uppsåt att det ska användas för att begå något av de brott som straffbeläggs i enlighet med artiklarna </SPAN><NOBR>2–5.</NOBR> En part får i lag uppställa krav på att flera sådana föremål ska innehas för att straffansvar ska gälla.</P>
<P class="p664 ft121"><SPAN class="ft128">2.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft142">Denna artikel ska inte tolkas som att den ålägger straffansvar i de fall där tillverkning, försäljning, anskaffning för användning, import, spridning eller annat tillgängliggörande eller innehav som avses i punkt 1 i denna artikel inte har till syfte att något av de brott som straffbeläggs i enlighet med artiklarna </SPAN><NOBR>2–5</NOBR> i denna konvention ska begås, såsom exempelvis för att i behörig ordning testa eller skydda ett datorsystem.</P>
<P class="p665 ft120"><SPAN class="ft128">3.</SPAN><SPAN class="ft138">Varje part får förbehålla sig rätten att inte tillämpa punkt 1 i denna artikel, om förbehållet inte avser försäljning, spridning eller annat tillgängliggörande av föremål som avses i punkt 1 a ii i denna artikel.</SPAN></P>
</DIV>
<DIV id="id_1_2">
<P class="p164 ft2">Prop. 2020/21:72 Bilaga 2</P>
</DIV>
</DIV>

<DIV id="id_1_2">
<P class="p223 ft120">Att mata in, ändra, radera eller undertrycka datorbehandlingsbara uppgifter så att icke autentiska uppgifter uppstår med uppsåt att dessa ska beaktas eller ligga till grund för handlande i rättsliga hänseenden som om de vore autentiska, oavsett om uppgifterna är direkt läsbara och begripliga. En part får uppställa krav på bedrägligt uppsåt eller liknande brottsligt uppsåt för att straffansvar ska gälla.</P>
